<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e26dcba8-aa15-41d1-9e20-6d3c9f5b3ebb'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7746255817106681082"><em>From a brilliant new talent comes a riveting novel of chance, fate, and numbers, and one man's strange journey past the boundaries of the possible.</em>David Caine inhabits a world of obsession, rich rewards, and rapid, destructive downfalls. A compulsive gambler and brilliant mathematician prone to crippling epileptic seizures, he possesses the uncanny ability to calculate odd</span>
  <span id="freeText7746255817106681082" style="display:none"><em>From a brilliant new talent comes a riveting novel of chance, fate, and numbers, and one man's strange journey past the boundaries of the possible.</em>David Caine inhabits a world of obsession, rich rewards, and rapid, destructive downfalls. A compulsive gambler and brilliant mathematician prone to crippling epileptic seizures, he possesses the uncanny ability to calculate odds of any hand in the blink of an eye. But one night at an underground poker club, Caine makes a costly misscalculation, sending his life spinning out of control. Desperate, he agrees to test an experimental drug with unnerving side effects: inexplicable visions of the past, present, and future. Unsure whether he's perceiving an alternate reality or suffering a psychotic breakdown, Caine embarks on a journey that stretches beyond the possible into the world of the improbable. Gradually, he discovers the extent of his astonishing new ability -- but powerful, shadowy forces know Caine's secret. Now Caine must fight for his survival -- and his sanity . . .</span>
  <a data-text-id="7746255817106681082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10102769008830028717">I have read it in Turkish so i am going to review it in two language))<br/>So, i've read Empaty first, and like Empaty , Improbable is one of the best sci-fiction books i have ever read!   <span id="freeText10102769008830028717" style="display:none">I have read it in Turkish so i am going to review it in two language))<br />So, i've read Empaty first, and like Empaty , Improbable is one of the best sci-fiction books i have ever read! I love sci-fiction, i am glad that Improbable gave me a lot of action, sci-fiction and excitement)) It made me love math more, which i never loved, love physics much more)) Laplace's devil? Wooww! I have never thought about deja vu and odds and a lot of futures which are waiting to happen and only happen because of our desicions))) The plot was the best of this book: action, complexity of events and real, solid characters are brilliant! Don't want to spoil anything, just to say something about characters:<br /> David Caine: our lovely protagonist)) Very clever, talented man who tries to make a"a happy end" for everyone after his failure on his life)) He is kind hearted, but also knows how to make sinciere desicions)) I loved this character so much, even he has some flaws like being gambler))<br /> Nava Vaner: Russian girl)) but unlike anyone else, she is a very talented spy))) Like everyone else in this book she also has some flaws but for the one AIM, she did her best! Even David Caine cannot make through without her))<br /> Jasper Caine: David's twin)) He has Schizophrenia but he is as talented as his brother)) I liked him too))<br /> Steven Grimes? hey, is he the one from Empaty? I am sure he is)))<br />For not being spoiler i stop the review)) This book is Excellent!<br /> Kitapın kurgusu, olayların gidişi, düşünceler, karakterlerin canlılığı ve özel olmaları))) Bu kitap bir baş yapıt! özellikle de fizik teorileri ve gelicek bir çok kaderler, olacaklar ve seçimlerimizin her şeyi nasıl etkilediyi... Bunları kitapı okudukdan sonra daha iyi anladım)) Çok memnunum ki, Adam Favver kendi hayallerinin peşinden koşmuş ve kitap yazarı olmaya karar vermiş)) Onu alkışlıyorum))) Kitapı çok insan Empati ile karşılaşdırıyor, ama bence her ikisi kendine göre muhteşem))</span>

<div id="review_113753474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113753474" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3971007-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461261523p2/3971007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113753474?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/3971007-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113753474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2017284500637641290">This book would make a kick-ass action movie. As a novel though, for what it was, it was great, as the plot was quick-paced and the action was intense. What it lacked was in-depth character development, as the characters were a little one-dimensional; there was the flawed nice-guy protagonist, the tough sexy girl, the crazy brother, the bad ass with a heart... and their motives were obvious and expected. BUT, for this novel it was more about the science and the action than the character developm</span>
  <span id="freeText2017284500637641290" style="display:none">This book would make a kick-ass action movie. As a novel though, for what it was, it was great, as the plot was quick-paced and the action was intense. What it lacked was in-depth character development, as the characters were a little one-dimensional; there was the flawed nice-guy protagonist, the tough sexy girl, the crazy brother, the bad ass with a heart... and their motives were obvious and expected. BUT, for this novel it was more about the science and the action than the character development, so it didn't really bring it down. I thought the idea behind the plot was pretty cool and the little explanations of the science for the layperson (eg. Leplace and probability theory) made it seem plausible, or should I say not <i> Improbable</i>, haha. Then again, I'm not a science person, so I can't attest to the reality of the science. Overall, the novel was entertaining and a fun summer read. Great for the beach!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2017284500637641290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7387079176264799958">I quite liked this odd little book. If you're a math person, you'll probably like it even more. If you liked Minority Report, you'll probably find something fascinating about this cause/affect plotline.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2541598886" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2541598886" />
    <a title="Paul Weiss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51664350-paul-weiss"><img alt="Paul Weiss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453113069p2/51664350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2541598886?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Weiss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Weiss" href="/user/show/51664350-paul-weiss">Paul Weiss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51664350-paul-weiss?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51664350-paul-weiss?shelf=physics">physics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51664350-paul-weiss?shelf=math">math</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2541598886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1454576359618444691"><b>Great science but the Byzantine plot is tough to follow!</b><br/><br/>David Caine, able to perform astonishingly complex mathematical calculations of probabilities and odds in his head, is a successful compulsive gambler. Playing on credit and beaten badly one night in a game of Texas Hold `Em by a lucky punter who pulled a Royal Flush on the River to trump his four bullets, Caine finds himself in debt to the Russian Mafia. When he suffers a massive grand mal temporal lobe epileptic seizure immediately after </span>
  <span id="freeText1454576359618444691" style="display:none"><b>Great science but the Byzantine plot is tough to follow!</b><br /><br />David Caine, able to perform astonishingly complex mathematical calculations of probabilities and odds in his head, is a successful compulsive gambler. Playing on credit and beaten badly one night in a game of Texas Hold `Em by a lucky punter who pulled a Royal Flush on the River to trump his four bullets, Caine finds himself in debt to the Russian Mafia. When he suffers a massive grand mal temporal lobe epileptic seizure immediately after losing the hand, he finds himself in the last ditch position of accepting the offer of a dangerous and highly experimental drug treatment in an effort to regain control of his life. Now hostage to the drug regimen, he finds himself unable to flee the Russians and is pulled into the web of a CIA investigation of his doctor's dangerous and unethical experimental drug treatments on unknowing human subjects.<br /><br />With the help of tough female rogue CIA agent Nava Vaner, Caine scrambles for his life and his sanity as side effects of the drugs give him visions and turn him in a real-life version of <i>"Laplace's Demon"</i> with the ability to tap into the collective unconscious, to see <i>"everywhen"</i>, the universe of innumerable myriad outcomes of the world's actions - in short, to know past and present and to affect and predict the future. And there are factions that will do anything to capture Caine to tap into and exploit that power!<br /><br />While the plot-line for <b>Improbable</b> can be fairly categorized as outstanding, Fawer's execution in this, his debut novel, falls prey to some typical first novel weaknesses. An overly large cast and excessively complicated plot twists will befuddle and frustrate all but the most attentive readers. Character development is a hit and miss affair, at best. Caine and his schizophrenic brother, Jasper, are fully fleshed out colourful protagonists with a credible, well-constructed set of fears, aspirations, flaws, emotions and strengths. On the other hand, Nava Vaner, comes across as weakly contrived and artificially inserted into the novel to serve as a mandatory female interest.<br /><br />But then there's the science that, almost magically, Fawer has dropped effortlessly into the maelstrom of a high-speed thriller ... and, my goodness, here is where Fawer excels! Literate, painless, crystal clear lay explanations of a wealth of seemingly un-related topics - biochemistry, schizophrenia, statistics, quantum mechanics, probability theory, "Laplace's Demon", DeMoivre's Theorem, chaos, Heisenberg's Uncertainty Principle, Jungian philosophy, Schrodinger's Cat, the birthday paradox and more. And, as wild as this may seem, all of it is used to quite reasonably propel the plot forward. (If Fawer ever decides to write a popular science non-fiction book, I'll snap it up in a heartbeat!)<br /><br />No doubt some readers will see <b>Improbable</b> as a five-star smash thriller. The plot confusion factor will almost certainly cause others to set it aside as a "did not finish". I'll call it three stars and anticipate that Fawer's next novel will reflect his deeper experience as a published author.<br /><br />Paul Weiss<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1454576359618444691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13862650939059009519" style="display:none">I'm always a little turned off by the idea of sci-fi... I want to like it, I'm just pretty sure I won't.   <span id="freeText6343709868613153512" style="display:none">Identical twins. Buff blonde Russian double agent. Nerdly geeks. North Koreans, KGB, NSA, CIA. Corruptible civil servants. Mob run card games. Scientists mad with ambition. Bodies vaulting from sixth floor labs. Remotely exploded cars. Surveillance vans with FedEx logos. Suitcases full of cash. Kidnappings and chase scenes. Migraines, brain spasms, preternatural prediction. Its all there. Its all pretty well written, so you could suspend your disbelief and ride the story. I did for a while, then it got corny, with not enough snappy humor to keep me in the game. So, I folded. Not a slam on the author who constructed a pretty good book. I was just in the mood for either more subtlety, or sex, or silliness. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13266708078225759665">Thanks to one of my GoodReads friends for recommending this book, which I'd never have come across otherwise. Oddly enough, the part of that reader's review that most attracted me to give the book a whirl was a complaint that the exposition of bits of probability theory was somewhat tedious. <i>Oooooo!</i> I thought. <i>Exposition of bits of probability theory! Sounds like my kinda thing . . .</i> And I was right. It's not just bits of probability theory you get but various quantum speculations, some history </span>
  <span id="freeText13266708078225759665" style="display:none">Thanks to one of my GoodReads friends for recommending this book, which I'd never have come across otherwise. Oddly enough, the part of that reader's review that most attracted me to give the book a whirl was a complaint that the exposition of bits of probability theory was somewhat tedious. <i>Oooooo!</i> I thought. <i>Exposition of bits of probability theory! Sounds like my kinda thing . . .</i> And I was right. It's not just bits of probability theory you get but various quantum speculations, some history of science and of psychoanalysis, lots of juicy goodness like that. And it's all tangled up in a fast-moving, often very witty SF/thriller novel. Really, this merits 4.5 stars. Much recommended.</span>

A came across it in a paperback format a long time ago and still cannot believe how such an amazing story and I hold the bar pretty high! I looked for the author everywhere and could not find anything he's written. What a disappointment for such a sharp and highly intelligent author!<br/>Bedouin </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FpWX7/2OKDPhJHZBtcYsUvk60a5Ht6nSOBxGLEzjAlbIVCJ9i5MlEjRDXOLuHK6QdSLIn20y/Fz6xu7Seui8rQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0RJl+DmdT2QLWrbXRsi1QhtVRO3RVS7Up22gdf5g5lQP09BqT4BCRd49nHQdEjeAl01d3PvQe1pltwiLyGtYrw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/84127.Adam_Fawer">About Adam Fawer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17758287632288038950">Adam Fawer (born 1970 in New York City) is an American Novelist. Improbable, his first novel, has been translated into more than five languages and won the 2006 International Thriller Writers Award for best first novel. His second novel, Empathy, has been published in 2008 in German, Japanese and Turkish.<br/><br/>Fawer holds undergraduate and master's degrees from the University of Pennsylvania and receive</span>
  <span id="freeText17758287632288038950" style="display:none">Adam Fawer (born 1970 in New York City) is an American Novelist. Improbable, his first novel, has been translated into more than five languages and won the 2006 International Thriller Writers Award for best first novel. His second novel, Empathy, has been published in 2008 in German, Japanese and Turkish.<br /><br />Fawer holds undergraduate and master's degrees from the University of Pennsylvania and received an MBA from the Stanford Graduate School of Business. During his corporate career, Fawer worked for a variety of companies including Sony Music, J.P. Morgan, and most recently, About.com, where he was the chief operating officer.<br /><br />Fawer lives in New York with his partner and two sons.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17758287632288038950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
